- **Why vault-mcp at T0.1.9 is structurally not in threat surface:** vault-mcp is a stdio **server** — spawned by a host (Claude Desktop, Cursor, future vault-tauri host functionality), reads stdin, writes stdout, does NOT spawn child processes. vault-mcp does not parse `StdioServerParameters` because that is a host-side data structure for telling a host which command to spawn. vault-mcp IS the spawned command, not a spawner of further commands. The April 15 RCE class therefore does not apply to vault-mcp's role at T0.1.9.
- **Decision:** Pin `rmcp = "=1.5.0"` in workspace `[workspace.dependencies]` (per BRD §2.9 / T0.1.5b discipline). No server-side mitigation work in vault-mcp at T0.1.9 because the threat surface doesn't apply. **Forward pointer (load-bearing):** when **T0.1.11 vault-tauri or successor task introducing MCP-host functionality** lands — specifically: passing user-controlled input into `StdioServerParameters` configuration (e.g. letting the user configure external MCP servers from the UI) — that task's plan **must address the April 15 RCE class threat surface per this ADR**. The §10 tech-debt entry is the operational cross-link.
- **Anthropic protocol-level posture:** Anthropic has declined to modify the protocol architecture, calling the behavior "expected" (per Hacker News writeup 2026-04-20). Mitigation responsibility lives at the integration layer (host-side use of `StdioServerParameters`), not in the protocol itself, and not in vault-mcp's server-side use.
- **Spike 1 acceptance #2 amended (per v1.3 Option A):** Originally required "canonical adversarial payload shape captured as concrete test data." Amended to: "scope analysis showing whether the threat surface applies to vault-mcp's role." The scope analysis above satisfies this. The adversarial-payload assertion is **NOT** carried forward into Phase 1 because writing it would be the **pass-for-wrong-reason** failure mode plan v1.2 §2 explicitly forbids — vault-mcp does not parse `StdioServerParameters`, that surface doesn't exist in our role, a test asserting "send malicious StdioServerParameters config to vault-mcp's stdin loop" would prove nothing.
- **Spike 1 acceptance #3 satisfied:** rmcp version pinned to `=1.5.0`.
- **Phase 1 deliverables landed in this ADR's commit:**
  1. This ADR.
  2. `rmcp = "=1.5.0"` exact-pin in workspace `Cargo.toml`.
  3. `initialize` round-trip runtime-confirmation smoke test in vault-mcp tests — boots `StdioServer`, sends JSON-RPC `initialize`, asserts response shape matches the spec. Surfaces any rmcp 1.5.0 API drift between web research and runtime, same way the ort 2.0.0-rc.10 ↔ ORT 1.22.0 coupling surfaced in T0.1.7 Phase 1.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Drop ADR, log April 15 RCE class as tech-debt entry only:* Rejected — pattern parity with ADR-015 + ADR-018 + ADR-025 (load-bearing architectural invariants belong in ADRs not tech-debt). Tech-debt entries decay because they sit in a list with N other items and get triaged by recency, not by load-bearing-ness. Future-Claude opening T0.1.11's plan needs the host-vs-server distinction immediately, not buried in a backlog.
  - *Full v1.3 redo of all surfaces:* Rejected — surfaces (2)–(5) of plan v1.2 are correct; only surface (1) needed the reframe. v1.3 was a focused diff against v1.2.
- **When to revisit:**
  - When T0.1.11 vault-tauri (or successor) lands MCP-host functionality — that task references this ADR + writes the actual mitigation per the threat model.
  - When OX Security or Anthropic publish protocol-level mitigation (so far Anthropic has declined; revisit if posture changes).
  - When rmcp publishes a version that introduces server-side stdio mitigation (e.g. defense-in-depth for spawn-time binary verification, even though our role doesn't strictly need it).
  - When a new CVE in the April 15 class affects rmcp's server-side surface specifically (we should re-scope vault-mcp at that point).
- **Cross-link:** T0.1.9_PLAN.md §2 (Spike 1 finding) + §3.1 (surface (1) reframed) + §9.1 (ADR-026 body shape) + §10 (tech-debt entry forwarding to T0.1.11).

### ADR-027 — 2026-05-02 — Pre-dispatch validation: tracing-only, no audit-chain append (T0.1.9 Phase 2 Step 5)

- **Context:** vault-mcp performs typed validation between rmcp's JSON deserialisation and handler dispatch. Today (Step 5): `parse_memory_id_traced` decodes the UUID strings carried by `tool_update` / `tool_delete` request bodies. Future tools may add schema-level checks at the same layer (numeric range validation, unicode-class restriction, etc.). These checks reject malformed requests before any handler runs. The architectural question: where do the rejection records go — the **audit chain** (tamper-evident, BRD §11.9, vault-state authoritative) or **tracing** (operational, BRD §11.5 logging, ops-tooling scope)?
- **Decision:** Pre-dispatch validation failures emit `tracing::warn!(target: "vault_mcp::request_validation", ...)` and **DO NOT** append to the audit chain. The audit chain is reserved for handler-dispatched vault operations per Q7(a) handler-mediated audit. The synthesised `ToolInvokeError::InvalidInput` audit-row variant is reserved for handler-internal validation that occurs *after* dispatch (e.g., a vault-storage layer rejecting input mid-cascade), not for pre-dispatch wrapper rejection. The wire-response mapping is unchanged: parse failures still return `McpError::invalid_params("invalid params", None)` (`-32602`) per ADR-024 line 765 — only the audit-append is skipped.
- **Reasoning:**
  - **(i) Q7(a) scopes audit to dispatches, not all rejections.** The audit chain's invariant is "every row is a vault-state transition outcome" (BRD §11.9 tamper-evident audit log + ADR-024's locked schema framing of `mcp.tool_invoke` as vault-dispatch accounting). A malformed-UUID request never reaches the vault; recording it as a vault-state transition would weaken the invariant for zero forensic gain.
  - **(ii) Symmetry with rmcp's JSON deserialisation rejection.** rmcp itself rejects bodies that fail JSON-RPC envelope parsing or fail to deserialise into the typed `Parameters<T>` wrapper — these never reach our handlers, and we don't audit them either. `parse_memory_id_traced` is one layer down (typed-but-string-encoded ID strings) but the same kind of pre-dispatch validation. Keeping the symmetry means the audit chain has exactly one consistent semantic: "the vault tried to do something, here's the result."
  - **(iii) Audit chain authoritativeness depends on consistent semantics.** "Every audit row is a vault dispatch outcome" is a stronger and more useful invariant than "every audit row is some rejection of some kind." The former lets a forensics user reconstruct vault state evolution from the audit chain alone; the latter pollutes that reconstruction with non-state-transition rejections.
  - **(iv) Operational forensics for adversarial probing live in tracing, not audit chain.** An attacker probing the API surface with malformed UUIDs to map authorisation boundaries or tool name space produces high-volume `vault_mcp::request_validation` warn events that ops-tooling (log aggregation, IDS correlation, rate-limit hooks at V0.2 per ADR-023 deferral) can pattern-match without bloating the per-user audit chain. Audit chain stays low-volume and high-signal; operational log carries the noisy edge.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Synthesise `ToolInvokeError::InvalidInput { message: "invalid id" }` and append audit on parse failure.* Rejected — expands Q7(a) scope to handler-side synthesis, blurs audit-chain semantics from "vault dispatch outcomes" to "some rejection of some kind," and shifts adversarial-probing forensics from ops-tooling (where the industry default lives) into the per-user audit chain. The reasoning would also apply, by extension, to JSON-deserialisation failures, which would balloon audit volume on adversarial probing.
  - *Append a separate `mcp.request_validation` audit event type (distinct from `mcp.tool_invoke`) for pre-dispatch rejections.* Rejected for V0.1 — the per-event-type schema cost is real (parse arm, wire-format string, hash-chain implications, divergence from ADR-024's locked `tool` enum), and no V0.1 forensic requirement justifies it. Re-considered if (a) below triggers a revisit.
  - *Tracing-only, no separate target.* Rejected — folding pre-dispatch parse failures into the same `vault_mcp::tool_invoke` target as dispatch records would tangle two semantically distinct event streams (dispatch-completed-ok-or-failed vs. dispatch-never-happened-because-malformed). Different targets keep ops-tooling filtering clean per Q5/Q6.
- **When to revisit:**
  - **(a) Compliance or forensic requirement** that demands tamper-evident pre-dispatch validation history (BRD §11.x update, regulatory pull). Two paths from there: extend the audit chain with a marker distinguishing dispatched-vs-rejected rows, or make tracing tamper-evident via a separate signed-log mechanism. Don't paper over the distinction silently.
  - **(b)** When pre-dispatch validation surface grows (e.g., more typed param structs gain custom decoders beyond UUID parsing) — re-confirm the discrimination still feels right. The decision scales naturally to additional decoders that follow the same shape; it may need re-examination if a decoder produces semi-structural rejections (e.g., a quota-related rejection that's neither pure malformedness nor a vault state transition).
  - **(c)** When the rate-limit hooks deferred per ADR-023 land at V0.2 — the rate-limiter likely consumes the same `vault_mcp::request_validation` tracing target as one of its inputs; verify the target naming + field shape stays useful.
- **Phase 2 test that proves it (Step 5):** `parse_failure_emits_tracing_does_not_append_audit` in `tests/tool_invoke.rs` — submit a `memory.delete` with a malformed UUID; assert (1) tracing event captured at `vault_mcp::request_validation`, (2) recording adapter's `recorded_audits().len()` is unchanged from baseline, (3) wire response is `-32602 "invalid params"` (the wire mapping per ADR-024 stays unchanged on parse failure).
- **Cross-link:**
  - ADR-024 (audit row schema — `InvalidInput` audit variant reserved for handler-side synthesis per this ADR; wire mapping `-32602 "invalid params"` is preserved across parse and handler-side InvalidInput paths).
  - ADR-025 (trust-boundary contract — pre-dispatch validation is at the transport boundary, post-dispatch handler validation is at the application boundary; this ADR specifies that audit-append happens at the application boundary, not the transport boundary).
  - BRD §11.7 (input validation at every public API boundary) + BRD §11.9 (tamper-evident audit log scope).
  - Feedback memory: "Inline architectural decisions produce an ADR in the same commit" (this ADR is itself an instance of that pattern — surfaced during Step 5 implementation, locked in the same commit).

### ADR-028 — 2026-05-02 — Memory update semantics: preserve provenance, overwrite content + classification (T0.1.9 Phase 2 Step 6)

- **Context:** `vault_storage::cascading::StorageBackend::update_memory` overwrites every field of `Memory` (per `tx_update_memory`'s `UPDATE memories SET content=?, memory_type=?, source_agent=?, boundary=?, created_at=?, valid_from=?, valid_until=?, confidence=?, access_count=?, last_accessed=?, superseded_by=?, metadata_json=?`). MCP-driven update (Step 6 `VaultAdapter::update`), future connector ingestion, and the V0.2 sync engine all need an update path that preserves provenance + lineage and only overwrites content + classification metadata. Naive overwrite from a freshly-constructed `Memory::try_new(NewMemory)` would silently destroy `created_at` (provenance), `access_count` (read-history → consolidation signal), and `superseded_by` (consolidation lineage — would break the V0.2 consolidator's chain). The decision needs to be locked at the contract layer, not embedded in one consumer's code.
- **Decision (rule statement):** **OVERWRITE only what the MCP write/update tool wire schema exposes** per ADR-024's tool-param contract — `content`, `memory_type`, `boundary`, `confidence` — **plus system-managed fields that update is expected to advance** (`last_accessed = Utc::now()`; `embedding` re-computed from new content). **Everything else PRESERVES** across update.
- **Decision (per-field classification table — Memory has 14 fields per `crates/vault-core/src/memory.rs:85-100` at this commit):**

  | # | Field | Type | Class | Reasoning |
  |---|---|---|---|---|
  | 1 | `id` | `MemoryId` | **PRESERVE** | Identity invariant — id IS the row, can't change across update. |
  | 2 | `content` | `String` | **OVERWRITE** | The literal change target — what the agent is updating. |
  | 3 | `memory_type` | `MemoryType` | **OVERWRITE** | Classification metadata; agent reclassification valid (semantic ↔ episodic ↔ procedural). |
  | 4 | `source_agent` | `Option<String>` | **PRESERVE** | Genesis attribution. The audit chain records per-invocation actor (`actor_kind = Agent` per ADR-025 Step 6 application) so "which agent did the update" is captured forensically without overwriting genesis. Conflating genesis with most-recent-author destroys the distinction silently. |
  | 5 | `boundary` | `Boundary` | **OVERWRITE** | Agent-supplied via `NewMemory`; subject to the StdioServer auth-gate check against the trusted `authorized_boundaries` slice (ADR-025). The agent CAN move a memory to a different authorized boundary. |
  | 6 | `created_at` | `DateTime<Utc>` | **PRESERVE** | Provenance. Destroying creation timestamp on update destroys the audit/forensic trail and the consolidator's age-based decay signal. |
  | 7 | `valid_from` | `DateTime<Utc>` | **PRESERVE** | Bi-temporal validity window. The MCP write/update wire schema does NOT expose `valid_from` (per ADR-024 `WriteToolParams` shape: `content` / `boundary` / `memory_type` / `source_agent` / `confidence` only). MCP can't update what MCP doesn't expose; preserving avoids silent reset to "now" on every MCP-driven update. |
  | 8 | `valid_until` | `Option<DateTime<Utc>>` | **PRESERVE** | Same shape as `valid_from` — MCP wire doesn't expose it. |
  | 9 | `confidence` | `f32` | **OVERWRITE** | Agent's assessment of the new content; updating content typically updates confidence. |
  | 10 | `access_count` | `u32` | **PRESERVE** | Read-history counter; consolidation signal. Resetting to 0 on update destroys consolidation input. (V0.1 has no read-side increment yet; the field is preserved for V0.2 consolidator readiness.) |
  | 11 | `last_accessed` | `DateTime<Utc>` | **OVERWRITE → `Utc::now()`** | Update IS an access; advancing `last_accessed` reflects the touch. |
  | 12 | `superseded_by` | `Option<MemoryId>` | **PRESERVE** | Consolidation lineage. Resetting on update breaks the V0.2 consolidator's chain. |
  | 13 | `embedding` | `Option<Vec<f32>>` | **OVERWRITE → re-computed** | Stale embedding is a correctness bug — content changed, vector must reflect new content. The re-compute fires through the same `EmbeddingProvider` used at write. |
  | 14 | `metadata` | `serde_json::Value` | **PRESERVE** | MCP wire schema does NOT expose `metadata`. Same shape as `valid_from` / `valid_until` — preserve to avoid silent wipe of metadata populated through other channels (manual entry, future connector ingestion). |

- **Reasoning:**
  - **(i) Provenance/lineage is irreversibly destroyed by naive overwrite.** Once `created_at` resets to "now," the original creation moment is gone — no audit row records the old value (ADR-024 logs the update event but not the old field values; the field is overwritten in-place). Same for `access_count` and `superseded_by`. The asymmetry is the right asymmetry: PRESERVE is reversible (a future ADR amendment can add OVERWRITE classification when a concrete consumer forces the question); OVERWRITE is not (once a destructive update path ships, every consumer downstream has to assume it can fire and write defensive code around it).
  - **(ii) MCP wire-schema-driven OVERWRITE keeps the classification rule contract-anchored and refactor-safe.** Naming the rule against the wire schema (ADR-024 tool-param contract — `content` / `memory_type` / `boundary` / `confidence`) rather than against a Rust struct name (`WriteToolParams`) means future Rust refactors don't break the ADR; future wire-schema extensions trigger ADR-028 amendment per the revisit triggers below.
  - **(iii) System-managed fields (`last_accessed`, `embedding`) advance because update IS a touch event.** Update without advancing `last_accessed` would mean "Tuesday's update doesn't show up in 'when was this last touched?'" Update without re-computing `embedding` is a correctness bug (stale vector against new content).
  - **(iv) The audit chain captures the per-invocation activity log via `mcp.tool_invoke` rows** (ADR-024 schema). The memory row's `source_agent` is genesis attribution; the audit chain's per-invocation `actor_kind` (ADR-025 Step 6 application) is current activity. Two distinct facts, two distinct fields, no conflation.
  - **(v) Bi-temporal + metadata fields preserve because MCP can't update what it doesn't expose.** A future MCP wire-schema extension that exposes `valid_from` / `valid_until` / `metadata` would trigger an ADR-028 amendment classifying those fields explicitly; until then, preserve avoids accidental data loss.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Naive overwrite (overwrite all fields from the supplied `NewMemory` via `Memory::try_new_with_id`).* Rejected — destroys provenance + lineage as enumerated above. Same correctness anti-pattern that vault-app would have to defensively work around at every consumer.
  - *TODO-marked err-stub deferring to T0.1.10.* Rejected — creates a known-incorrect state someone has to remember to fix; same anti-pattern as the work-breakdown drift catches at Step 4 and Step 5. T0.1.10 owns lifecycle/config, not contracts; update semantics is a contract decision and lives at the contract layer (this ADR), not the consumer's TODO list.
  - *Partial-merge semantics for `metadata` (deep-merge incoming keys into existing, instead of preserve).* Rejected — fails the forward-compat-pull test (no concrete consumer requires partial-merge today; manual entry and future connectors populate via different code paths, neither blocked by Step 6's preserve default). Partial-merge has real semantic complexity (merge strategy: deep / shallow / key-collision rules / null-as-delete) deserving its own ADR if and when a concrete consumer forces the question. Preserve today is reversible; locking partial-merge today is not.
- **When to revisit:**
  - **(i) MCP write/update tool wire schema extension adds a new field** — classify the new field in an ADR-028 amendment; align the implementation in the same commit as the schema extension.
  - **(ii) `Memory` struct gains a new field in `vault-core`** — classify in an ADR-028 amendment with reasoning. **Default to PRESERVE if classification is non-obvious** and surface for review; the safe direction is the easy direction. The default-to-PRESERVE-on-new-field rule makes the failure mode (new field leaks through naive overwrite) hard to introduce silently; OVERWRITE classification requires explicit approval.
  - **(iii) BRD provenance or temporal-validity contracts update** — re-confirm the classification still aligns with the updated provenance/temporal model.
  - **(iv) V0.2 introduces concurrent MCP dispatch or sync-engine writes** — re-evaluate the read-before-write race surface (currently V0.1 single-user serial MCP doesn't fire the race; V0.2+ may need read-update inside one SQLite transaction, which would extend ADR-016 connection-ownership / ADR-017 cascade-FIFO).
- **Cross-link:**
  - ADR-024 (audit row schema — update events appear in `audit_log` per the existing chain; the `mcp.tool_invoke` row records the update invocation, this ADR governs what the row's target memory looks like after update).
  - ADR-025 (trust-boundary contract — `boundary` overwrite is allowed per this ADR but must pass the StdioServer auth-gate check; the auth-gate site is at the handler layer, not the adapter).
  - ADR-027 (audit-vs-tracing scope — update preservation is a vault-state concern, audited per ADR-024 `mcp.tool_invoke` event).
  - Q2 carry-forward (VaultAdapter minimal-at-Step-6 — this ADR is the contract VaultAdapter implements at Step 6).
- **Phase 2 test that proves it (Step 6):** `vault_app::adapter::tests::update_preserves_provenance_per_adr_028` — pre-populate a memory with non-default `created_at` (2025-01-15), `access_count = 42`, `superseded_by = Some(other_id)`, custom `metadata`, `source_agent = "genesis-agent"`, `valid_from = 2024-06-01`. Call `Adapter::update` with new `content` + `memory_type` + `boundary` + `confidence` + a different `source_agent` (`"update-agent"`) + a different `metadata`. Assert (a) PRESERVED fields (`source_agent`, `created_at`, `valid_from`, `access_count`, `superseded_by`, `metadata`) unchanged; (b) OVERWRITTEN fields (`content`, `memory_type`, `boundary`, `confidence`) match input; (c) `last_accessed` advanced past the pre-update timestamp; (d) embedder called once during update (re-compute pinned).

---

## Tech Debt Backlog

Items noticed but not addressed in their originating task — picked up explicitly when scheduled, never as drive-by work.

- [x] ~~**(T0.1.9 Phase 3 Step 2 — IN FLIGHT) Linux CI disk-space exhaustion at `libduckdb-sys` archive step**~~ — **DONE 2026-05-03 across `306453b` (Step 2a, free-disk-space@main) + `ca4c190` (Step 2b, actions/cache + setup-dev-env.sh fixture provisioning).** Both runs CI-green-verified via `gh run list -L 2`. Step 2a recovered the compile path; Step 2b's surfaced-then-fixed test-phase fixture absence (`embedding_tests.rs:38-44` loud-panic-not-silent-skip) closed the full pipeline. 22-commit silent-failure stretch (2026-04-30 13:40 UTC → 2026-05-03 closure) resolved. See "### Step 2a + 2b — closure record" subsection above for full record. **Forward concern (open):** `jlumbroso/free-disk-space` recovers ~15-20 GB, ample today; if `libduckdb-sys` or heavy build deps continue to grow, may need more substantial intervention (cache strategy, build-feature trimming, larger CI runner). Track if disk margin tightens again post-2b. (Noted 2026-05-03, closed 2026-05-03; files: `.github/workflows/ci.yml`, ADR-001 cross-link)
- [ ] **(2026-05-04, V0.2 hardening forward concern) Graceful disk-full handling on user device** — Memory Vault writes go to SQLite/SQLCipher metadata + LanceDB vectors + DuckDB graph + (post-T0.1.6) retry-queue overflow to `pending_sync`. **Disk-full failure mode is currently unspecified** — no explicit error path, no user-facing surface, no in-flight rollback story. ADR-010 / BRD §11.5 cover encryption-at-rest correctness; disk-full handling is a separate operational concern. **Likely failure shape:** SQLite returns `SQLITE_FULL` (rusqlite `Error::SqliteFailure(..., DiskFull)`); LanceDB's underlying object_store returns IO error; cascading orchestrator's three-table-atomic invariant (per ADR-016) means a partial-write at the LanceDB layer leaves SQLite + audit_log committed but vector store missing — same write→search invisibility class that Phase 1b's spike caught for a different root cause. **Required behavior at V0.2 hardening:** (1) detect `SQLITE_FULL` and IO-error-on-write at orchestrator scope; (2) fail the write with a clear `VaultError::DiskFull(...)` variant — pattern-matchable, distinct from `Storage(String)` grab-bag; (3) MUST NOT corrupt in-flight state — orchestrator's transaction discipline (ADR-016) gives us atomic abort, but verify that LanceDB's failure mode matches; (4) surface to user via Tauri error toast / banner with concrete action ("free up disk space and try again — your data is safe"); (5) log at WARN level with structured fields (path, available bytes, attempted size). **Test requirements:** integration test that simulates disk-full via a low-quota tmpfs / loopback-mount fixture, asserts (a) write fails with `VaultError::DiskFull`, (b) no partial state left in SQLite/LanceDB/DuckDB, (c) subsequent writes after disk freed succeed. **Why V0.2 hardening, not V0.1:** founder dogfood at T0.1.12 won't realistically hit disk-full on a developer machine (unbounded disk); 30-user beta cohort at T0.2.16 includes users on more constrained hardware (older laptops, partitioned drives) where this becomes a real concern. **Cross-link:** related to T0.2.0 LanceDB encryption-at-rest work — both touch the storage write path; consider coordinating the disk-full path with T0.2.0's `lance::ObjectStore` adapter design so the IO-error surface is unified across plaintext-vs-encrypted paths. (Noted 2026-05-04, files: `crates/vault-storage/src/cascading.rs::cascading_write`, `crates/vault-core/src/error.rs` for new `DiskFull` variant, `crates/vault-tauri` for user-facing error surface)
- [ ] **(T0.1.10 session-open, 2026-05-04) macOS CI matrix entry — land at T0.1.11** — Three-platform CI matrix is a V0.1 internal-alpha promise (ADR-001 originally predicted "Add macOS to the matrix in T0.1.7"; actual sequence shipped Linux at T0.1.9 Phase 3 Steps 2a+2b and Windows at Step 2c, leaving macOS the final third). T0.1.11 (vault-tauri minimal UI) is the right landing target — Tauri ships native macOS `.app` bundles via ADR-019's `load-dynamic` ort strategy (per-platform `libonnxruntime.dylib`), and BRD §11.7.5 mandates release-time signing on macOS, both of which are vault-tauri-shaped concerns.
  - **Tactical patch shape:** add `macos-latest` to `strategy.matrix.os` on `clippy` + `build-and-test` (`fmt` stays single-runner). Existing fixture-cache step already keyed on `runner.os`, so cache slot is automatic. New step: `if: runner.os == 'macOS'` invoking a new `scripts/setup-dev-env-macos.sh` (or extended `setup-dev-env.sh` with `case $(uname -s)`) that fetches `onnxruntime-osx-arm64-1.22.0.tgz` instead of the Linux/Windows tarballs. No `jlumbroso/free-disk-space` call (Linux-only). No Strawberry Perl prerequisite — macOS ships system Perl that satisfies openssl-src.
  - **Notable macOS-specific concerns to validate at T0.1.11 plan time:**
    - **(a)** `macos-latest` resolves to `macOS-15-arm64` as of **2026-05-04 verification** against `actions/runner-images` README (https://github.com/actions/runner-images — the "macOS 15 Arm64" row maps `macos-latest`, `macos-15`, or `macos-15-xlarge` to image `macOS-15-arm64`); ort 1.22.0 ships arm64 + x86_64 native binaries, pick arm64. **Re-verify at T0.1.11 plan time** — the runner-images README explicitly notes that GitHub Actions migrates the `-latest` label across OS versions over 1–2 month windows, so a future macOS bump (e.g., `macos-26-arm64` if promoted to `-latest`) keeps arm64 architecture but may shift OS version; if the README's `macos-latest` row has changed at T0.1.11 landing, re-verify the ORT URL pattern + update `setup-dev-env-macos.sh` accordingly. **Note:** `macos-latest-large` is the x64/Intel variant per the same README — do NOT use it (we want arm64 for ort native + Apple Silicon dogfood parity).
    - **(b)** `aarch64-apple-darwin` toolchain auto-installed by `dtolnay/rust-toolchain`.
    - **(c)** `libonnxruntime.dylib` SHA-256 is distinct from Linux/Windows — `MODEL_PROVENANCE.md` table needs a third row.
    - **(d)** Any test failing macOS-only → root-cause, NOT `#[cfg(not(target_os = "macos"))]` skip per the standing rule.
  - **Floor forecast:** 0 new tests. Workspace stays at whatever T0.1.10 closes at on each matrix entry. Success metric: TWO consecutive green CI matrix runs across `[ubuntu-latest, windows-latest, macos-latest]`.
  - **Why T0.1.11 not T0.1.10:** T0.1.10 is vault-app wiring (no platform-specific surface beyond what T0.1.9 already proved); adding macOS matrix during T0.1.10 bundles unrelated CI infra into a wiring task. T0.1.11 is the natural fit (Tauri bundling + signing surface) and pre-T0.1.12 dogfood is the latest acceptable point per the V0.1 alpha promise. (Noted 2026-05-04, ADR-001 cross-link, files: `.github/workflows/ci.yml`, `scripts/setup-dev-env*.sh`, `MODEL_PROVENANCE.md`)
- [ ] **(T0.1.10 Phase 2a, 2026-05-04) `VaultError::WorkerSpawnFailed` variant re-evaluation at V0.2 alpha cut** — Variant added in Phase 2a (`crates/vault-core/src/error.rs`) per session-open pre-flag #5 to keep startup-fatal failure modes pattern-matchable distinct from `McpBindFailed`. **Currently unreachable as of Phase 2a**: `RetryWorker::new` is infallible struct construction and `tokio::spawn` is infallible; no fallible step in the worker spawn path right now. Reserved for future fallible spawn paths (bounded-thread-pool spawning, config-driven worker startup, worker-side resource acquisition that returns `Result`). **Re-evaluation milestone:** at V0.2 alpha cut, audit whether a concrete consumer has surfaced; if not, REMOVE the variant + the corresponding exhaustive-match arms in `vault-mcp::vault_error_to_mcp` and `vault-mcp::ToolInvokeError::from_vault_error`, and re-add only when concretely needed. Concrete-vs-hypothetical test (`feedback_forward_compat_concrete_vs_hypothetical.md`) applied to the variant's own existence — pinning the milestone prevents dead-code accumulation. (Noted 2026-05-04, files: `crates/vault-core/src/error.rs`, `crates/vault-mcp/src/server.rs::vault_error_to_mcp`, `crates/vault-mcp/src/audit.rs::from_vault_error`)
- [ ] **(T0.1.10 Phase 2a, 2026-05-04) MCP server graceful-shutdown — V0.1 known limitation, V0.2/V1.0 work** — `ApplicationHandle::shutdown` aborts the running MCP server task rather than closing the rmcp stdio transport gracefully. In-flight tool calls are dropped on shutdown. Closing stdin from inside the process is not directly supported by rmcp's stdio transport at version `=1.5.0`; a future-proof graceful-MCP shutdown would require either (a) a transport-level close API in rmcp, OR (b) a supervisor pattern that closes stdio externally (e.g., parent process holds the pipe ends). Acceptable for V0.1 internal alpha (single-user, single-agent, founder dogfood T0.1.12). **Revisit triggers (any):** (1) V0.2 multi-agent task pins concurrent-MCP-call drain semantics; (2) V1.0 GA hardening adds a graceful-shutdown SLO; (3) rmcp 1.x adds a transport-level close API (check rmcp release notes during the monthly tech-debt cron). **Documented at the code site** in `crates/vault-app/src/application.rs::ApplicationHandle::shutdown` doc-comment + here for project-level audit-trail queryability. (Noted 2026-05-04, files: `crates/vault-app/src/application.rs::ApplicationHandle::shutdown`)
- [ ] **(T0.1.9 model spike, 2026-05-03) 512-token context ceiling vs T0.2.x connector ingestion** — bge-small-en-v1.5's 512-token max sequence becomes a concrete constraint at T0.2.x connector ingestion (BRD §5.9). Long emails, PDFs, transcripts, conversation logs may routinely exceed 512 tokens; current naïve right-truncation strategy loses tail content. **Re-spike trigger:** T0.2.x connector ingestion task kickoff. **Primary candidate:** `nomic-embed-text-v1.5` (8192-token native context, Matryoshka truncation 768→512→256→128→64 — preserves the LanceDB schema with minimal migration, Apache-2.0). Trade-offs to evaluate: ~3× param count vs latency budget, mandatory `search_query:` / `search_document:` prefix injection (BgeSmallProvider API redesign), no first-party ONNX export (would weaken ADR-019 chain). **NOT a present-day switch trigger.** V0.1 manual-entry workflow stays well under 512 tokens for typical memories. (Noted 2026-05-03, T0.1.9_MODEL_SPIKE.md §6.1)
- [ ] **(T0.1.9 model spike, 2026-05-03) Annual model-currency re-check** — bge-small-en-v1.5 was released September 2023 (~2.5 years old as of this spike). SOTA in small-class English embedding shifts roughly yearly; don't assume the lock holds across multi-year intervals. **Re-run cadence:** re-run this spike at **V0.2 release** and again **before V1.0 GA**. Same matrix structure applies; refresh candidate list (e.g., Jina v5-small, Qwen3-embedding-small, whatever sits at MTEB head at the time). Even if no candidate dethrones bge-small at re-check, the verification is what makes the lock trustworthy. (Noted 2026-05-03, T0.1.9_MODEL_SPIKE.md §6.2)
- [ ] **(T0.1.9 model spike, 2026-05-03) Future-swap evaluation criteria — locked** — If a future model swap is ever evaluated, apply criteria in order: (1) **license clean for commercial closed-source distribution** — hard pass/fail; (2) **first-party ONNX export** from the model author, not community-converted — hard requirement for ADR-019 trust posture; community ONNX requires its own re-verification path; (3) **prefix-injection compatibility with `BgeSmallProvider`'s API surface** OR explicit `BgeSmallProvider` API-surface amendment + downstream propagation through vault-retrieval — models requiring mandatory prefixes (e5 family, nomic family, etc.) trigger an explicit amendment phase before the swap, not silent integration; (4) **MTEB-R parity or improvement** vs the 51.68 NDCG@10 baseline — sub-baseline retrieval requires explicit justification; (5) **≤ 512 MB ONNX disk size** for installer-fatness budget — larger requires ADR-amendment + V1.0 download-progress UX revisit per BRD §6 V1.0 installer concerns. (Noted 2026-05-03, T0.1.9_MODEL_SPIKE.md §6.3)
- [ ] **(T0.1.9 Phase 3 Step 2) CI green is distinct from local DoD gates — verification required at every commit** — The 22-commit silent-failure stretch happened because we treated CI green as implicit-from-the-fact-that-CI-runs. Going forward, per-step commit confirmation must include explicit CI green check (`gh run list --workflow=ci.yml -L 1` showing `success` on the previous push), not just local gates green. Local DoD gates (build / test / clippy / fmt / `--no-run` link) prove the code passes on the founder's Windows dev machine; CI green proves it passes on a clean-room Linux runner. Both verifications are necessary; neither alone is sufficient. Queued as **CLAUDE.md candidate #8** (provisional name `feedback_ci_green_distinct_from_local_dod_gates.md`); promotion gate is sustained green CI across Step 2a + 2b + 2c plus a few subsequent T0.1.10 commits. **Don't promote prematurely** — pattern needs to demonstrate it works in practice. (Noted 2026-05-03, cross-link to "## CI Discipline Recovery" section)
- [ ] **(T0.1.9 Phase 1) chrono pin advance 0.4.38 → 0.4.39** — bumped at T0.1.9 Phase 1 to satisfy `rmcp 1.5.0 → schemars 1.0`'s hard transitive `chrono ^0.4.39` requirement. ADR-013 amended. **Revisit at:** every chrono / arrow-arith / lance update (verify the underlying `Datelike::quarter()` ↔ `ChronoDateExt::quarter()` conflict surface hasn't migrated to chrono 0.4.39+; if arrow-arith fixes the qualified-call site upstream, we can drop the pin entirely). Same monthly cadence as ADR-013's existing chrono CVE check. (Noted 2026-05-01, file: `Cargo.toml` workspace `chrono` pin)
- [ ] **(T0.1.9 Phase 1) `#[tool_router(server_handler)]` + `#[tool]` macro wiring on `vault-mcp::StdioServer`** — deferred from Phase 1 to Phase 2. Phase 1 `StdioServer` has plain async `handle_*` methods that exercise trust-boundary discipline + auth-gate validation; Phase 2 wraps them with rmcp's macros for actual tool dispatch over JSON-RPC. **Why deferred:** rmcp 1.5.0's macro contract (`Parameters<T>` wrapper, return-type mapping, `serde::Deserialize`-only-vs-`schemars::JsonSchema` requirement, error mapping into `CallToolResult`) isn't well-documented beyond a single README snippet; deciphering it correctly is best done alongside the real handler bodies in Phase 2 rather than against `unimplemented!()` stubs. **Phase 2 work:** wire macros, replace stub adapter with real `VaultAdapter` from vault-app (T0.1.10), remove should_panic markers, add full JSON-RPC `initialize` round-trip test + the `dimension_mismatch_returns_generic_invalid_params_with_full_audit_detail` ADR-024 test, append `mcp.tool_invoke` audit events at handler exit per ADR-024 schema. (Noted 2026-05-01, files: `crates/vault-mcp/src/server.rs`, `crates/vault-mcp/tests/initialize_smoke.rs`, `crates/vault-mcp/tests/trust_boundary.rs`)
- [ ] **(T0.1.9 Phase 1) rmcp `schemars` cargo feature deliberately excluded** — Phase 1 lands `rmcp = "=1.5.0"` with features `["server", "macros", "transport-io", "transport-async-rw"]` only. The `schemars` feature pulls additional surface (the `JsonSchema` derive macro for our user code) but ALSO exposes new chrono surface that conflicts with our pin even at 0.4.39. The feature stays off until: (a) the chrono pin can advance further (post-arrow-arith fix), OR (b) Phase 2's macro wiring confirms it doesn't need user-side `JsonSchema` derives. Production `vault-mcp` Phase 1 uses bare `serde::Deserialize` for `SearchToolParams` / `WriteToolParams`. (Noted 2026-05-01, file: `crates/vault-mcp/Cargo.toml`)
- [ ] **(T0.1.9 ADR-026) April 15 RCE class threat surface forwarded to future MCP-host task** — OX Security advisory 2026-04-15 (CVE-2025-65720, CVE-2026-30623, CVE-2026-30624, CVE-2026-30615, CVE-2026-26015, CVE-2026-30618, CVE-2026-33224, CVE-2026-30617, CVE-2026-30625, CVE-2026-40933, CVE-2025-49596, CVE-2025-54994, CVE-2025-54136 — full list per ADR-026). - [ ] **(Recurring) Monthly rustc pin revisit** — `rust-toolchain.toml` pinned to `1.92.0` (post-T0.1.6a CI green). **Reason:** rustc 1.95.0 tightened the trait-solver depth limit; `lance 0.15.0` exceeds it (`error: queries overflow the depth limit!` while compiling `lance::dataset`). Same drift class as ADR-013's chrono pin. **Revisit triggers (any):** (a) lance bumps to a version that compiles on newer rustc; (b) a Critical / High Rust security advisory affects 1.92.0 (RustSec / blog.rust-lang.org); (c) we drop lance for a different vector store; (d) we want to use a 1.93+ language feature in our own code. **Operational follow-up:** first Monday of each month, check https://blog.rust-lang.org for advisories affecting 1.92.0 + check lance's GitHub for releases that compile on newer rustc. If neither: hold the pin. If a security advisory hits and lance hasn't unblocked, evaluate forking lance or switching vector stores. (Noted 2026-04-30, file: `rust-toolchain.toml`)
- [ ] **DuckDB 1.2.2 autocommit-INSERT wedge on UNIQUE constraint violation** — Discovered during T0.1.5: `Connection::execute("INSERT INTO entities ...", ...)` against a row that violates the composite UNIQUE `(name, entity_type, boundary)` does NOT return an error promptly — it wedges the connection indefinitely (test hung >5min, killed). Worked around in `DuckDbGraphStore::create_entity` by pre-checking with `SELECT COUNT(*)` inside an explicit transaction before the INSERT (the explicit-tx + pre-flight pattern avoids the wedge). The pre-check + insert is atomic because we hold the connection mutex for the whole tx. **Operational follow-up:** revisit on every duckdb-rs minor bump — if a fix lands upstream, drop the pre-flight check and rely on a single INSERT with native UNIQUE-violation error mapping (cleaner code + one less round-trip). Tracked here so future-us doesn't quietly inherit the workaround as canon. (Noted 2026-04-30, file: `crates/vault-storage/src/graph_store.rs` `create_entity`)

Adding `* text=auto eol=lf` plus binary markers for known binary file types would silence the CRLF warnings on commit and make cross-platform behaviour deterministic. Quick win when convenient. (Noted 2026-04-28)

- [ ] **`VaultError::Storage(String)` grab-bag — split into structured variants** (per ADR-018 / Phase C plan v2 closing note). The cascading orchestrator's `is_permanent` classifier currently substring-matches `Storage(msg).contains("schema")` to recognise schema-mismatch errors. That works but defeats type-safe matching. Future ADR: split into structured variants — `VaultError::SchemaMismatch { table: String, detail: String }`, `VaultError::IoFailure(...)`, etc. — so `is_permanent` becomes an exhaustive match. Knock-on: every `VaultError::Storage(format!(...))` site in vault-storage gets re-categorised. Estimated touch: ~30 sites across `metadata_store.rs` / `vector_store.rs` / `graph_store.rs` / the cascading + retry modules. Plan: schedule as a stand-alone refactor task (not a drive-by) at the start of T0.2.x — by then we'll have a fuller picture of which error categories actually matter from the consolidator + sync angles. Until then, `is_permanent` substring-matching stays as documented in the classifier doc-comment. (Noted 2026-04-30, ADR-018, files: `crates/vault-core/src/error.rs` + `crates/vault-storage/src/retry_queue.rs`)
- [ ] **`pending_sync` sweep — extend schema with cascade payload (migration 0003 at T0.2.x)** — Phase A intent for the divergence detector's `pending_sync` sweep was to drain rows back into `retry_queue` when capacity returns. The migration 0002 schema only carries `(memory_id, operation, queued_at)`, so the sweep can't reconstruct the `NewRetry` payload (embedding + boundary). For V0.1 the sweep is a stub that always returns 0; cap-overflow is unrealistic at V0.1's expected scale (≤ tens of thousands of memories), so the stub is acceptable. **Real impl** at T0.2.x adds a small migration `0003_pending_sync_payload.sql` that ALTERs `pending_sync` to add `embedding BLOB NOT NULL DEFAULT X'' (zeroed-default for legacy rows; legacy rows are unreachable in production because V0.1 is local-only and pre-dogfood)` + `boundary TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT ''`. The orchestrator's overflow path then writes the full payload; `DivergenceDetector::sweep_pending_sync` re-enqueues into `retry_queue` while `RetryQueue::len() < MAX_RETRY_QUEUE_DEPTH`. Estimated touch: ~80 LoC + tests. (Noted 2026-04-30, file: `crates/vault-storage/src/divergence.rs` `sweep_pending_sync`, gates on `crates/vault-storage/src/migrations/`)
- ⚙️ **AUTOMATED via `.github/workflows/monthly-tech-debt.yml`** (added 2026-04-30) — covers cargo audit (RustSec database, catches most CVEs across all transitive deps automatically) + version-pin verification (ort↔ORT, chrono, rustc, openssl-src, protoc) + auto-opens a GitHub issue with the report. Auto-fires first Monday of each month at 09:00 UTC; also manually triggerable via Actions UI (`workflow_dispatch`). The recurring entries below are still authoritative for what each check means + what action to take when findings surface — the workflow surfaces the data; the user makes the call. Close each month's auto-opened issue when checks are complete.

- [ ] **(Recurring) Monthly ort RC-policy + ONNX Runtime release-notes check + setup-script ORT_VERSION verification** — `ort = "=2.0.0-rc.10"` is a tactical pin, similar to ADR-013's chrono `=0.4.38`. **Reason:** ort is still in 2.0 release-candidate (latest as of 2026-04-30 is rc.12); rc.12 has a build error against ort-sys (`OrtApi.SessionOptionsAppendExecutionProvider_VitisAI` field missing) — rc.10 is the latest known-good RC for our use. **The ort crate version is tightly coupled to a specific ONNX Runtime native-lib version** (encoded via `ort_sys::ORT_API_VERSION`); ort `2.0.0-rc.10` requires ORT `1.22.x`. `scripts/setup-dev-env.{sh,ps1}` pins `ORT_VERSION = "1.22.0"` to match. Same drift class as the chrono pin. **Revisit triggers (any):** (a) ort 2.0 stable releases — bump to 2.0.x, **also bump setup-dev-env scripts' ORT_VERSION to whatever ort's release notes say it bundles**; (b) a newer rc.X fixes the VitisAI build issue — bump together with setup script ORT_VERSION; (c) Critical/High CVE in onnxruntime native lib (https://github.com/microsoft/onnxruntime/security/advisories) affecting our pinned ort-sys version — evaluate forward-bump-vs-mitigate, bump setup script ORT_VERSION accordingly.
  - **Operational procedure (concrete commands, cadence: first Monday of each month, runs alongside the existing OpenSSL / protobuf / chrono / rustc monthly checks per ADR-006 / ADR-011 / ADR-013 / `rust-toolchain.toml` tech-debt entry):**
    1. **Inspect resolved `ort` + `ort-sys` versions in our lockfile:**
       ```bash
       cargo tree -p vault-embedding --depth 0 -e normal | grep ort
       grep -A1 '^name = "ort"' Cargo.lock
       grep -A1 '^name = "ort-sys"' Cargo.lock
       ```
    2. **Read setup script's `ORT_VERSION` (Bash + PowerShell — both must agree):**
       ```bash
       grep -E '^(ORT_VERSION|\$OrtVersion)' scripts/setup-dev-env.sh scripts/setup-dev-env.ps1
       ```
    3. **Cross-check against ort release notes** — visit https://github.com/pykeio/ort/releases/tag/v<our-pinned-rc> and grep the page for "ONNX Runtime v" (release notes always announce the bundled ORT version, e.g. "Updated to ONNX Runtime v1.22.0").
    4. **If they disagree:** the script's `ORT_VERSION` is the source of truth for what we ship; bring `ort` crate version into agreement, OR bump `ORT_VERSION` to match ort's bundled. Re-run `scripts/setup-dev-env.{sh,ps1}` to refresh the dylib + re-run `cargo test -p vault-embedding test_concurrent_init_succeeds` (and tests 1, 2, 5) to confirm runtime compatibility.
    5. **If they agree** (expected, no-op month): record "ort RC-policy check OK 202X-MM-DD" and move on.
  - **Next due:** 2026-06-01 (first Monday of June). Tracked here in HANDOFF.md tech-debt — the same place the OpenSSL / protobuf / chrono / rustc checks live. (Noted 2026-04-30 + concrete commands added 2026-04-30; files: `Cargo.toml` `ort` workspace dep + `scripts/setup-dev-env.{sh,ps1}` `ORT_VERSION`/`$OrtVersion`)

- [ ] **vault-retrieval perf gate — investigation deferred to post-T0.1.10** (Noted 2026-05-01, T0.1.8 Phase 3 finding, file: `crates/vault-retrieval/tests/retrieval_tests.rs::end_to_end_retrieval_latency_under_200ms_with_1k_memories`)
  - **Surfacing context:** First end-to-end run of `vault-retrieval`'s perf gate landed in T0.1.8 Phase 3 (2026-05-01) on Shahbaz's Windows dev box, idle machine + fresh build cache, T0.1.7 measurement methodology. Phase 1 had `retrieve()` as `unimplemented!()` so this gate would have panicked if invoked; Phase 2 left it `#[ignore]`-d. **First two runs:** 412ms (run 1), 1,852ms (run 2). Both well over the 200ms BRD §5.5 retrieval ceiling. Runs 3–5 killed because each setup phase took 200–600s — see "setup phase issue" below. NB: the "84ms" measurement we discussed across Phase 1 → Phase 3 was vault-**embedding**'s `test_6_embed_within_100ms_budget` (single bge-small embed call, 100ms ceiling), not this gate — they were always the same test as T0.1.7's 12.3ms median, methodology-driven variance, both passing the embedder ceiling.
  - **Suspected cause (not proven):** LanceDB fragmentation. The perf-gate setup does 1000 individual `vectors.upsert` calls, which creates 1000 fragments. Without an explicit vector index, LanceDB falls back to per-fragment full-scan cosine k-NN, and search latency grows roughly `O(fragments × rows_per_fragment)`. The 384-dim cosine math itself is cheap — the cost is fragment scanning + per-fragment file I/O on Windows.
  - **Production implication:** **This is NOT a synthetic-fixture artefact.** V0.1's production write path writes memories one-at-a-time too (each `StorageBackend::write_memory` is one `vectors.upsert`). After 1000 production memories accumulate, the same fragmentation should manifest. The gate surfaces a real V0.1 perf concern that founder-dogfood T0.1.12 will hit at moderate vault sizes if not addressed.
  - **Investigation candidates** (post-T0.1.10, when integration smoke gives realistic data):
    - **Explicit vector index** in `LanceVectorStore::open` — LanceDB supports IVF + HNSW; pick one based on V0.1's expected vault size and recall/latency trade-off. Largest-impact intervention; needs benchmarking.
    - **Compaction lifecycle** — call `LanceVectorStore::compact` periodically (e.g., on startup if fragment count exceeds a threshold, or via a maintenance task in vault-app). Reduces fragments → reduces per-search scan cost. Cheaper than indexing but doesn't change asymptotic cost.
    - ~~**Bulk-insert in tests**~~ — **REJECTED** because it'd hide the production concern. Production writes one-at-a-time; the gate's fixture should reflect that.
  - **Right time to investigate:** post-T0.1.10. Reasoning: T0.1.10 (vault-app wiring) is where `BgeSmallProvider × LanceVectorStore × MetadataStore` first integrate end-to-end with the cascading orchestrator + audit chain + retry queue all live. The integration-risk spike planned for T0.1.10 will give us realistic perf data on actual workload patterns (not 1000-memory synthetic loops). Investigating now means optimising against synthetic fixtures that may not represent the real workload.
  - **Setup-phase issue (separate concern, worth tracking):** the test's 1000-insert setup loop took **200–600 seconds per run** on Windows — that's 200ms–600ms per insert. That's surprisingly slow for SQLite + LanceDB on a modern dev box; suggests the *write* path also has fragmentation or per-call overhead worth investigating (each `create_memory` is its own SQLite tx with audit append; each `vectors.upsert` is its own LanceDB write). Could surface as a separate tech-debt item ("V0.1 write-path latency on Windows") if T0.1.12 founder-dogfood feels sluggish on individual writes.
  - **What stays in the codebase as the contract pin:** the `assert!(elapsed.as_millis() < 200, ...)` line in the test stays load-bearing — when the investigation lands and indexing/compaction is wired, the gate is the verification that the fix works. The `#[ignore]` reason string explicitly cites the Phase 3 measurements + this tech-debt entry so the next person to look at the test understands the history without re-deriving it.
- [ ] **(Recurring) Monthly `tokenizers` upgrade-compatibility check (per ADR-022)** — `tokenizers = "=0.20.4"` is exact-pinned with `default-features = false, features = ["onig"]`. The trim drops `esaxx_fast` (pulls `esaxx-rs` /MT, conflicts with duckdb-sys /MD at MSVC link) and `progressbar` (training-time UI). When upgrading tokenizers (any version bump), the trim's compatibility must be re-verified — a feature rename or a previously-gated import losing its gate could silently break compile or runtime behaviour. **Operational procedure (cadence: first Monday of each month, alongside OpenSSL / protobuf / chrono / rustc / ort per `.github/workflows/monthly-tech-debt.yml`):**
  1. **Inspect resolved `tokenizers` version + `esaxx-rs` presence:**
     ```bash
     cargo tree -p vault-embedding -e normal | grep -E "tokenizers|esaxx|onig|indicatif"
     ```
     `esaxx-rs` may still appear in the tree as a transitive entry but should NOT be compiled (no `.rlib` artefact in `target/debug/deps/` that contributes objects to the test binary). The proof is the link succeeding, not the absence of the line.
  2. **Run vault-embedding's full test suite + perf gate:**
     ```bash
     cargo test -p vault-embedding
     cargo test -p vault-embedding -- --ignored  # perf gate (test 6)
     ```
     All 9 active tests + 4 unit tests + `test_concurrent_init_succeeds` must pass; perf gate stays under the 100ms BRD §5.3 ceiling. `test_9_embed_uses_cls_pooling_not_mean_pooling` is the load-bearing tokenization-drift detector.
  3. **Run vault-retrieval test build (the original blocker):**
     ```bash
     cargo build -p vault-retrieval --tests
     ```
     Must finish without LNK2038 / LNK1319.
  4. **If any fail:** revisit ADR-022's "When to revisit" triggers. Likely fixes: re-add a feature that was renamed; pin tokenizers back; or fall back to ADR-022's Option B (`crt-static` rustflags). Document in ADR-022.
  5. **If all pass** (expected, no-op month): record "tokenizers feature-trim check OK 202X-MM-DD" and move on.
  - **Next due:** 2026-06-01 (first Monday of June). Tracked here in HANDOFF.md tech-debt — the same place the OpenSSL / protobuf / chrono / rustc / ort RC-policy checks live. (Noted 2026-05-01, ADR-022, files: `Cargo.toml` `tokenizers` workspace dep)

Before opening Step 7, complete Step 6's commit per the per-step commit contract. Sequence:

   ```

   ```

2. **Re-run DoD gates fresh** (the prior-session results above are informational; the discipline requires fresh gate-passing at commit time):
   - `cargo build --workspace -j 1` — zero warnings.
   - `cargo test -p vault-core` then `-p vault-cli` then `-p vault-storage` then `-p vault-embedding` then `-p vault-retrieval` then `-p vault-mcp` then `-p vault-app` — all `-j 1`. Fall back to per-crate if workspace fails.
   - `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -j 1 -- -D warnings` — zero warnings.
   - `cargo fmt --all --check` — clean.
   - `cargo test --workspace --no-run -j 1` — final test-binary-link assurance (the gate that the prior session did not complete).

3. **If any gate fails, STOP and escalate.** Do not commit pre-failure state. The DoD-gates-clean-at-commit-time rule is non-negotiable per Phase 2's locked discipline.

4. **If all gates pass, surface to Shahbaz the staging summary** (file list + test count + brief commit message draft) and request commit + push approval. Combined-approval rule (`feedback_confirm_before_commit_push.md`) applies once approval is given: commit + push without re-asking.

### T0.1.10 — next session opener (READ THIS FIRST)

**Where you are when you wake up:** working tree clean, `origin/main` at the T0.1.9-close roll-forward (this commit). Run `git status --short` to confirm clean tree. **T0.1.9 fully shipped** — vault-mcp Adapter + Stdio Server complete, sustained CI green across `[ubuntu-latest, windows-latest]` matrix verified across the final two commits. Three V0.1 tasks remain to internal alpha: T0.1.10 (this task), T0.1.11 (vault-tauri minimal UI), T0.1.12 (founder dogfood e2e).

**T0.1.10 scope (BRD §5.10):** wire `vault-app::Application` — the composition root that glues `BgeSmallProvider × StorageBackend × LanceDB × DuckDbGraphStore × MetadataStore × SemanticRetriever × VaultAdapter × StdioServer` together. Lifecycle: config load → dependency construction → cascading retry worker spawn → MCP server start → graceful shutdown on signal.

**Inheritances from prior tasks (T0.1.10 picks these up):**
- **Deferred Phase 4 integration smoke from T0.1.7** (`BgeSmallProvider × StorageBackend::write_memory` end-to-end against real LanceDB/SQLCipher; previously deferred per BRD §2.4 because vault-embedding ⊥ vault-storage and the integration belongs in vault-app).
- **Cascading retry worker lifecycle wiring from T0.1.6** (`Application::start` constructs `tokio::sync::watch::channel(false)`, spawns `worker.run(rx)`, signals cancel from `Application::shutdown`).

- **Adversarial integration coverage forward-pointer from T0.1.9 Phase 3 Step 1** — integration-level adversarial tests tracing dispatch end-to-end through real composed system (oversized query / max_results / NUL-in-query inputs reaching SemanticRetriever's validation chain through the real adapter, not fixture-bypassed).
- **Retrieval perf-gate investigation candidate from T0.1.8 Phase 3** — first end-to-end run on Shahbaz's Windows dev box measured 412ms / 1,852ms (well over the 200ms BRD §5.5 ceiling) with suspected LanceDB fragmentation. T0.1.10's integration-risk spike is the right place to measure on realistic workload data + decide on intervention (explicit vector index vs. compaction lifecycle).

**Discrete decisions to make at T0.1.10 session-open before any code:**

1. **CLAUDE.md candidate #8 promotion-to-default decision.** Data-point threshold reached during T0.1.9 (4 discrete CI-verified data points across 2 distinct CI tactic-stability questions: disk-cleanup tactic via 2a+2b on `25281167500` + `25282711557`; Windows matrix via 2c on `25283197434` + `25285317001`). Deferred from T0.1.9 close to T0.1.10 session-open as separate scope. Decision: promote `feedback_ci_green_distinct_from_local_dod_gates.md` to documented default (per-step commits include explicit `gh run list -L 1` CI-green check), OR keep candidacy with additional T0.1.10 data points required first. **Recommendation pending T0.1.10 session-open formal decision; prior here is *promote* based on four data points across two distinct CI tactic-stability questions, but the formal decision applies the candidate #8 evaluation criteria as written, not a cross-walk summary.** A recommendation is a starting position for formal evaluation, not a pre-baked conclusion.

2. **T0.1.10 plan-iteration depth.** Per the saved-feedback memory ("Plan-iteration depth scales with design-surface size"): T0.1.10 is a **consume-existing-contracts task** — composes already-locked traits/types from vault-mcp / vault-storage / vault-embedding / vault-retrieval. **One iteration + optional spike** is appropriate; not a 2-3 iteration contract-establishing task.

3. **Integration-risk spike methodology declaration** (per saved-feedback memory "Spike methodology explicit per spike"). Declared methodology: **compile-and-run** — wires the full chain end-to-end against real LanceDB / SQLCipher / ort, surfaces unknowns; this absorbs T0.1.7's deferred Phase 4 integration smoke by *being* the integration. **Stop-and-escalate trigger conditions (enumerated, not slogan)**: **(a)** any contract mismatch between two crates that compiled in isolation but doesn't compose at runtime (e.g., a `Result<T, E>` shape misaligned across a trait boundary; an `Arc<dyn Trait>` requiring `Send + Sync` where a concrete impl missed it); **(b)** any audit-chain hash discontinuity across the cascading boundary (BLAKE3 chain integrity per BRD §11.9.2 must hold across composition as it does in isolation); **(c)** any `spawn_blocking` deadlock or starvation pattern under retriever async load (embedder runs on `spawn_blocking`, retriever holds the runtime — pathological patterns surface only under composition, not unit tests); **(d)** any boundary-validation gap where memory from boundary A reaches retrieval results in boundary B (mandatory access control per BRD §11.4.3 — defense-in-depth proven in isolation at vault-storage; must hold end-to-end through adapter dispatch). Each trigger fires "stop, surface, no paper-over."

**Standing rules live throughout T0.1.10:**
- Per-step commit confirmation includes explicit CI green check (`gh run list --workflow=ci.yml -L 1` showing `success` on the previous push). Local DoD gates necessary but not sufficient.
- Any platform-specific failure during T0.1.10's integration runs → root-cause investigation, NOT `#[cfg(unix)]` / `#[cfg(windows)]` skip.
- Any unexpected runtime behavior → stop and escalate per the spike-methodology / runtime-confirmation pattern.
- Every commit + push needs explicit Shahbaz approval per CLAUDE.md.

**T0.1.10 forward concerns to track during planning:**
- After T0.1.10 lands, the retrieval perf-gate measurement re-runs cleanly under T0.1.7 methodology (5 consecutive runs, idle machine, post-fresh-build) on integration-realistic data. Either the 412ms/1,852ms result reproduces (real LanceDB fragmentation concern, intervention needed) OR it returns to the embedder's 12.3ms-class (synthetic-fixture artefact, no concern). Both outcomes inform whether T0.2.x needs to land an explicit vector index.
- ADR-010 V0.1 plaintext-on-disk HARD GATE before T0.2.16 — vault-app must surface the alpha-mode WARN log (compensating control #3). T0.1.11 lands the UI banners (compensating controls #1 + #2).

---

### T0.1.10 — session-open decisions landed (2026-05-04)

The three discrete session-open decisions enumerated above ("Discrete decisions to make at T0.1.10 session-open before any code") landed this date. Original questions retained for audit-trail history (asked 2026-05-03 at T0.1.9 close, answered 2026-05-04 at T0.1.10 session-open).

**Decision 1 — CLAUDE.md candidate #8 promote-to-default: DEFER FORMAL PROMOTION + PROVISIONAL ADOPT FOR T0.1.10.**

⚠ **PLAN AMENDMENT FLAGGED** — prior recommendation in the next-session opener was *promote*, based on a cross-walk of "4 data points across 2 distinct CI tactic-stability questions." Applying candidate #8's evaluation criteria as written (line 1422 verbatim: *"Don't promote until the candidate has demonstrated it works for vault-code commits, not just CI workflow changes"*), the formal decision flips to **defer**. Every existing data point (`306453b` Step 2a / `ca4c190` Step 2b / `76a75be` Step 2c / `9f83ba1` Phase 3 close roll-forward / `97dee57` next-opener roll-forward / `51546ca` macOS entry) is either a CI workflow change or doc-only — zero vault-code commits in the data set, which is precisely what the criterion forbids promoting against.

**Provisional adoption rule, live for T0.1.10's duration:** every Phase 1 / Phase 2 / Phase 3 commit must run `gh run list --workflow=ci.yml -L 1` after the previous push and confirm `success` before staging the next. Local DoD gates necessary but not sufficient. After T0.1.10 closes with at least 3 vault-code data points accumulated (Phase 1 spike commit + Phase 2 lifecycle commit + Phase 3 perf-gate commit, minimum), formally amend CLAUDE.md and promote candidate #8 to documented default; until then, candidate #8 stays in candidacy with this provisional adoption noted.

**Decision 2 — Plan-iteration depth: ONE ITERATION + INTEGRATION-RISK SPIKE (Phase 1).**

T0.1.10 is a consume-existing-contracts task per the saved plan-iteration-depth memory — composes already-locked traits/types from vault-core / vault-storage / vault-embedding / vault-retrieval / vault-mcp, no new contracts to establish. One iteration is appropriate; not 2-3 iterations like T0.1.5–T0.1.8 contract-establishing work. The integration-risk spike absorbs T0.1.7's deferred Phase 4 integration smoke (`BgeSmallProvider × StorageBackend::write_memory` end-to-end against real LanceDB/SQLCipher) by virtue of natural composition-root surface — the integration *is* the spike.

**Decision 3 — Integration-risk spike methodology: COMPILE-AND-RUN.**

Per the saved spike-methodology memory. Phase 1 produces an executable artefact that wires the full chain end-to-end against real LanceDB / SQLCipher / ort.

**First plan-time decision (deferred deliberately, not by default):** the artefact's exact form — `crates/vault-app/examples/integration_smoke.rs` example-binary vs `crates/vault-app/tests/integration_smoke.rs` `#[ignore]`-by-default integration test. Real downstream consequence to each: example-binary keeps the spike artefact discoverable as standalone runnable scaffolding (T0.1.7 pattern, lower friction for re-running ad-hoc); `#[ignore]`-test integrates with cargo test discipline + CI workflow gating (closer to standard test discipline, can be promoted to non-ignored when stability proves out). **Pick deliberately at plan time, not by default.**

**Four stop-and-escalate triggers, each with pre-declared detection method:**

- **(a) Contract mismatch** between two crates that compiled in isolation but doesn't compose at runtime — *detected via runtime panic OR trait-bound compile failure when the composed dep graph is first instantiated.*
- **(b) Audit-chain hash discontinuity** across the cascading boundary — *detected via end-to-end `audit_chain_verify()` call after the spike's write+retrieve sequence (BLAKE3 chain integrity per BRD §11.9.2 must hold across composition as it does in isolation).*
- **(c) `spawn_blocking` deadlock or starvation** under retriever async load — *detected via `tokio-console` instrumentation OR wall-clock-vs-CPU-time divergence on the spike's perf measurement (embedder runs on `spawn_blocking`, retriever holds the runtime — pathological patterns surface only under composition).*
- **(d) Boundary-validation gap** where memory from boundary A reaches retrieval results in boundary B — *detected via the spike's deliberate cross-boundary write+retrieve probe: write a personal-boundary memory, query from a work-boundary, expected zero results (mandatory access control per BRD §11.4.3 — defense-in-depth proven in isolation at vault-storage; must hold end-to-end through adapter dispatch).*

Each trigger fires "stop, surface, no paper-over."

**Phase 3 perf-gate outcome branching, pre-declared:**

- **(i) Reproduces** within 50% of T0.1.8's 412/1,852ms range → fragmentation/index hypothesis confirmed → log T0.2.x explicit vector index intervention as priority-zero tech-debt with the new measurements baked in.
- **(ii) Dispels** (returns to ~12ms embedder-class) → synthetic-fixture-artefact hypothesis confirmed → log resolution against existing T0.1.8 ignored-perf-gate tech-debt entry, un-ignore the perf-gate test with integration-realistic methodology baked into the test setup so future regressions surface against the right baseline.

---

### T0.1.10 Phase 1 — scaffold lands; integration finding surfaced; fix as Phase 1b (2026-05-04)

**Phase 1 scaffold landed:**
- `crates/vault-app/src/application.rs` (NEW, ~150 lines) — `Application::new` minimum composition surface. Wires the full V0.1 dep graph (`BgeSmallProvider × StorageBackend × LanceVectorStore × DuckDbGraphStore × MetadataStore × SemanticRetriever × VaultAdapter`) against real backends. No lifecycle / MCP server bind / retry-worker spawn — Phase 2 scope.
- `crates/vault-app/src/lib.rs` — export `Application`; V0.1-progress doc-comment update.
- `crates/vault-app/tests/integration_smoke.rs` (NEW, ~395 lines) — 4 `#[ignore]`-by-default `#[tokio::test]` triggers (a/b/c/d) per session-open Decision 3's compile-and-run methodology with pre-declared detection methods + Phase 1's 5-run spike-gate green definition (trigger (c) explicitly: ALL 5 under threshold; ANY single run over = stop-and-escalate, NO flake-retries).
- Workspace count: **364 passing + 6 ignored** (+4 from the four trigger tests, **floor hit exactly** per Phase 1 forecast).

**Spike execution: 5 consecutive `cargo test -p vault-app --test integration_smoke -- --ignored --nocapture` runs.**

**Per-trigger results (across all 5 runs, deterministic — no flake):**

| Trigger | Verdict | Surface |
|---|---|---|
| (a) contract mismatch | ✅ GREEN (5/5) | dep graph composes; method dispatch through `dyn Trait` chain end-to-end |
| (b) audit-chain hash discontinuity | ❌ FIRING (5/5) | **NOT what it was built to catch.** `verify_audit_chain` PASSED — multi-handle BLAKE3 chain integrity holds. Failure on the **post-audit retrievability sanity check** (line 271): `memory written through VaultAdapter::write MUST be retrievable through Adapter::search via SemanticRetriever` |
| (c) `spawn_blocking` deadlock/starvation | ✅ GREEN (5/5 under threshold) | no pathological pattern; concurrent_elapsed within 5x baseline×8 margin per pre-declared green definition |
| (d) boundary-validation gap | ❌ FIRING (5/5) | **NOT what it was built to catch.** Failure on the **negative-control assertion** (line 422 — added at session-open architecture review per discipline-flag #5): `personal-boundary search MUST find the personal-boundary memory`. Negative control caught a "retriever pathway broken" failure that would have silently passed the boundary-leak check |

**Unified root pattern (third, distinct integration finding):**

Writes through `VaultAdapter::write` (cascading orchestrator path: `StorageBackend::write_memory`) are not visible to subsequent reads through `VaultAdapter::search` (SemanticRetriever path: `SemanticRetriever::retrieve`). Two separately-designed triggers ((b)'s post-audit sanity check + (d)'s negative-control) caught the same finding via their secondary checks — defense-in-depth on test design, vindicated empirically.

**Phase 1b investigation order (user-confirmed):**

1. **(Cheap-disprove first)** `RetrievalOptions::default()` `score_threshold` filtering everything — single logging line at the retriever's inner search call discriminates "returned-but-filtered" vs "not-returned-at-all" in one test run.
2. **(Most-likely if H3 disproved)** Multi-handle SQLite metadata visibility — `StorageBackend` writes go through its internal `MetadataStore` connection; `SemanticRetriever` reads through a separate `Arc<MetadataStore>` (handle 3 in `Application::new`). SQLite/SQLCipher WAL behavior across separate connections may not expose recent writes without explicit checkpoint or transaction discipline.
3. **(If H1 disproved)** `LanceVectorStore` upsert-vs-query commit semantics — `vectors.upsert` may write to a buffer not visible to subsequent `query` calls until commit/flush.
4. **(Least likely)** `SemanticRetriever` boundary-filter inverted — existing vault-retrieval tests would have caught.

**Investigation methodology (per session-open Decision 3):** compile-and-run with explicit logging, NOT source-reading-only. Print raw `vector_store.search` results before `SemanticRetriever`'s filtering; print `MetadataStore` connection-level WAL state; print write's commit confirmation. Empirical-first, hypothesis-confirmation-second.

**Phase 1b scope discipline (user-flagged at this commit):** Phase 1b contains ONLY the fix for the unified root pattern. No drive-by refactoring of `Application::new` handle pattern beyond what the fix requires. No opportunistic `AppConfig` migration. No pre-emptive Phase 2 lifecycle work. **Additional findings during investigation become Phase 1c or get logged as forward-concerns; they don't bundle into Phase 1b silently.**

**Fix-location decision DEFERRED until root cause named** (per user discipline-flag): premature architectural decision. Fix lives in vault-storage IF root cause is multi-handle (H1); in vault-storage's vector path IF root cause is LanceDB upsert semantics (H2); in `Application::new`'s `RetrievalOptions` construction IF root cause is default `score_threshold` (H3). When root cause is named, surface fix-location options to user with architectural reasoning per option; don't pre-commit on "feels cleanest."

**Spike's defense-in-depth design — empirically vindicated:** months of contract-establishing work (T0.1.5–T0.1.9) composed cleanly enough that triggers (a) + (c) passed first try. Triggers (b) + (d) each carried a secondary check beyond their primary detection method (negative-control on (d) added during scaffold review per session-open architecture-flag #5; post-audit retrievability sanity check on (b) was Claude Code's design choice during scaffold drafting). Both secondary checks fired on the same root pattern. Single-trigger design would have either silently missed the bug (boundary leak masked by retriever absence) or surfaced it under the wrong attribution (audit-chain mistakenly blamed). Defense-in-depth on test design proved its value here, not theoretically.

**Phase 1b commit lands when:** root cause named via empirical investigation → fix-location options surfaced to user with architectural reasoning → user approves fix-location → implementation lands → 5-run spike re-execution shows ALL 4 triggers green.

---

### T0.1.10 Phase 2a — lifecycle increment shipped (2026-05-04)

**Path α confirmed at session-open** (two methods, no bool flag): `Application::start()` stays worker-only (test-focused, Phase 1b backwards compat); new `Application::start_with_mcp(authorized_boundaries)` for production lifecycle. Reasoning: bool-flag drift is real failure mode; test-vs-production divergence is honest, not a code smell; existing `integration_smoke.rs` empirical artefact stays untouched.

**Sub-phasing emerged from implementation findings** as 2a (lifecycle) / 2b (AppConfig) / 2c (adversarial) per the candidate-#8 data-point math + cohesion-vs-separability signals: lifecycle is genuinely cohesive (~210 lines, 6 files, all bound by `start_with_mcp`/`ApplicationHandle`/`shutdown`/signal-handler invariant); AppConfig migration + adversarial coverage are clearly separable. Bundling would conflate three independent decision categories into one review surface. Three discrete commits = three discrete data points (Phase 2a lands as data point 3; threshold met for candidate #8 formal-promotion decision at T0.1.10-close session).

**What landed:**
- `crates/vault-core/src/error.rs` (+18) — `VaultError::WorkerSpawnFailed` + `McpBindFailed` variants per session-open pre-flag #5 (distinct pattern-matchable variants, NOT generic `StartupFailed` bucket).
- `crates/vault-mcp/src/server.rs` + `crates/vault-mcp/src/audit.rs` (+8 / +15) — exhaustive-match extensions in `vault_error_to_mcp` and `ToolInvokeError::from_vault_error` for the two new variants. Privacy-preserving silent-collapse + Internal-collapse with explicit category names respectively.
- `crates/vault-app/Cargo.toml` (+9) — `rmcp` direct dep with `["server", "transport-io"]` features. Already transitive via vault-mcp; making explicit per Path α discipline (avoid vault-mcp-API-wrapper complexity for one consumer).
- `crates/vault-app/src/lib.rs` — `ApplicationHandle` export.
- `crates/vault-app/src/application.rs` (+170) — `start_with_mcp`, `ApplicationHandle` struct, `ApplicationHandle::shutdown` (consumes self by value), `handle_signals` (cross-platform `tokio::signal::ctrl_c` per docs.rs/tokio/1.52.1 verification), forced-exit semantics (`std::process::exit(130)` + stderr message after first-SIGINT graceful didn't complete).

**Empirical answers to session-open pre-flag #5:**
- **`McpBindFailed`: REACHABLE** — `rmcp::ServiceExt::serve()` returns `Result`. `start_with_mcp` synchronously awaits it, mapping `Err` → `VaultError::McpBindFailed("rmcp serve: {e}")`. Real (rare) failure path for transport setup errors.
- **`WorkerSpawnFailed`: TECHNICALLY UNREACHABLE at Phase 2a landing** — `RetryWorker::new` infallible struct construction; `tokio::spawn` infallible. Variant kept as future-proof per user (a) decision with V0.2 alpha cut re-evaluation milestone (see Tech Debt Backlog entry).

**`ApplicationHandle::shutdown` consumes self by value — locked reasoning:** terminal lifecycle methods consume `self` to enforce single-call semantics at compile time. Calling `shutdown` twice would attempt to re-await already-consumed `JoinHandle`s (panic). Consuming `self` rejects double-shutdown statically via the borrow-checker — structural correctness through API design, no runtime guard needed. Pattern echoes the Path α discipline (explicit divergence over hidden flexibility).

**Cross-platform signal handling — verified:** `tokio::signal::ctrl_c` works on both Unix and Windows under tokio's `signal` feature (enabled via workspace `tokio = { version = "=1.52.1", features = ["full"] }` line 40). Verified directly against `docs.rs/tokio/1.52.1/tokio/signal/fn.ctrl_c.html` 2026-05-04: *"While signals are handled very differently between Unix and Windows, both platforms support receiving a signal on 'ctrl-c'. This function provides a portable API for receiving this notification."* No `cfg(unix)` / `cfg(windows)` gating needed.

**V0.1 known limitation (logged as tech-debt for V0.2/V1.0):** MCP server shutdown aborts in-flight tool calls rather than closing the rmcp stdio transport gracefully. Documented at the code site (`ApplicationHandle::shutdown` doc-comment) AND project-level audit-trail (Tech Debt Backlog entry). Acceptable for V0.1 internal alpha; revisit at V0.2 multi-agent or V1.0 GA hardening, or sooner if rmcp adds a transport-level close API.

**Verification:** workspace count unchanged at 364 + 6 ignored. Existing 4 integration triggers ✅ on sanity run (no regression). Local DoD gates clean (fmt, clippy, build, test).

**Phase 2a forward-concerns logged for Phase 2b/2c (not bundled):**
- Phase 2b: AppConfig migration with strict rename prohibition (preserve seven Phase 1 inline param names verbatim).
- Phase 2c: 4 adversarial integration tests, each docstring anchored to its T0.1.9 Phase 3 Step 1 forward-pointer entry.
- `start_with_mcp` itself not exercised by Phase 2a's test diff — exercised by production main() at T0.1.11+ (vault-tauri); founder dogfood (T0.1.12) is the integration signal.
- Comprehensive per-variant audit test for Internal-collapse coverage — logged previously as Phase 2 forward concern; not bundled into 2a.

**Provisional candidate #8 data-point tracking:**
- dp1: `e3d2e7a` (Phase 1) ✅ CI green
- dp2: `0fdba30` (Phase 1b) ⏳ CI green confirmation pending at Phase 2a stage time
- dp3: this commit (Phase 2a) — lands data point 3
- **Threshold for formal CLAUDE.md candidate #8 promotion = min 3 vault-code data points; met as of this commit's CI green.** Formal-promotion DECISION available at T0.1.10-close session (NOT retroactively bundled into Phase 2a). dp4 = Phase 2b, dp5 = Phase 2c — five total by T0.1.10-close.
