### T0.1.10 Phase 1b — retry-worker fix shipped (2026-05-04)

**Root cause locked (none of the four pre-ranked hypotheses):** `cascading_write` (vault-storage/src/cascading.rs:456-533) writes to SQLite metadata + audit_log + retry_queue but **never calls `vector.upsert`**. Vector store updates happen asynchronously via `RetryWorker::run` (vault-storage/src/retry_worker.rs:189) draining `retry_queue` → `vector.upsert`. Phase 1's `Application::new` deliberately deferred worker spawn to Phase 2 (per the next-session-opener inheritance enumeration). Without the worker running, writes via `VaultAdapter::write` landed in SQLite + retry_queue but never propagated to vector_store, so `SemanticRetriever`'s vector-store-first query (semantic.rs:159) returned empty.

**Hypothesis evaluation (in order from session-open):**

| Hypothesis | Verdict | Method |
|---|---|---|
| H3 — default `score_threshold` filtering | **Disproved by source-reading** (no test run needed). `RetrievalOptions` derives `Default`; `score_threshold: Option<f32>` defaults to `None`; pipeline filter at semantic.rs:195-198 only applies under `Some(_)`. |
| H1 — multi-handle SQLite WAL visibility | **Disproved by source-reading** + existing passing test `vault-app/src/adapter.rs::write_embeds_then_cascades` proves cross-handle visibility. Empirical H1 refutation added to trigger (b) as regression check (3-line `metadata_for_assert.get_memory(id).expect(Some)` block). |
| H2 — LanceDB upsert/query commit semantics | **Refuted as misframed** — `cascading_write` never calls upsert in the first place; there's nothing to commit. |
| H4 — boundary filter inverted | **Refuted as misframed** — same 5/5 deterministic empty-result pattern across BOTH `personal` and `work` boundaries; if filter were inverted, one would pass. |
| H5 (surfaced via source-reading) — **retry-worker not spawned** | **Confirmed.** Source-reading the call graph from `VaultAdapter::write` → `StorageBackend::write_memory` → `cascading_write` revealed the missing `vector.upsert` call. `RetryWorker::run` is the missing link. Phase 1's `Application::new` doesn't spawn it. |

**Methodology divergence — self-flagged before proceeding** (saved as `feedback_source_read_call_graph_upstream_of_empirical.md`): user's pre-declared methodology was "compile-and-run with explicit logging, empirical-first." I caught the divergence (relying on source-reading instead) and surfaced it before acting. User accepted the divergence: "in this specific case, source-reading didn't bypass empirical discipline — it short-circuited an empirical investigation that would have been chasing wrong hypotheses anyway." Empirical confirmation in trigger (b) preserves the discipline literally where it costs nothing.

**Fix scope — Option B (locked at user direction):**
- ✅ `crates/vault-app/src/application.rs`: + `storage: StorageBackend` field on `Application`; clone for VaultAdapter; original retained for `start()` to clone into the worker.
- ✅ `crates/vault-app/src/application.rs`: + `pub fn start(&self) -> tokio::sync::watch::Sender<bool>` — constructs `tokio::sync::watch::channel(false)`, builds `RetryWorker::new(self.storage.clone())`, spawns `worker.run(rx)`, returns `tx`. Sender-drop = clean worker exit per `cancel.changed()` Err arm at retry_worker.rs:206.
- ✅ `crates/vault-app/tests/integration_smoke.rs`: + `setup_application` calls `application.start()`; `TestApp` holds the returned `Sender` (drop = clean shutdown).
- ✅ `crates/vault-app/tests/integration_smoke.rs`: + `wait_for_cascade_drain()` helper (3s sleep, covers 1s default poll × 2 cycles + processing margin); + empirical H1 refutation in trigger (b).

**NOT in Phase 1b** (per user scope-discipline reinforcement): shutdown handling logic, MCP server bind, signal handler registration, `AppConfig` migration, error recovery for worker-spawn failure, await-aware `Application::shutdown()` path. **Each is Phase 2 scope.**

**Forward concern logged for Phase 2 (not bundled silently):** Phase 2 may want a deterministic `Application::flush()` method that drains retry_queue synchronously for tests, replacing the 3s sleep heuristic in `wait_for_cascade_drain()`. Justified only if Phase 2 surfaces a concrete consumer; Phase 1b does NOT add it speculatively.

**Verification — 5-run spike re-execution (deterministic, no flakes):**

| Trigger | Run 1 | Run 2 | Run 3 | Run 4 | Run 5 | Verdict |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| (a) contract mismatch | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | **GREEN 5/5** |
| (b) audit-chain hash discontinuity | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | **GREEN 5/5** (was 0/5 pre-fix) |
| (c) `spawn_blocking` deadlock/starvation | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | **GREEN 5/5** under threshold |
| (d) boundary-validation gap | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ | **GREEN 5/5** (was 0/5 pre-fix) |

Run 1 41.3s (cold ort init); runs 2-5 7-8s each (cache warm). Workspace count unchanged: **364 + 6 ignored**.

**Discipline patterns vindicated this Phase:**
1. **Negative-control on trigger (d)** caught a finding neither trigger was designed to catch (added at session-open architecture review per discipline-flag #5).
2. **Self-flagging methodology divergence** preserved empirical-first instruction's *intent* even when literal application would have chased wrong hypotheses.
3. **Source-reading the call graph upstream of empirical experiments** corrected a four-hypothesis ranking that was 100% wrong about root cause — saved as new memory pattern.

**Provisional candidate #8 — second vault-code data point lands at this commit.** Phase 1's `e3d2e7a` was the first; Phase 1b's commit is the second. Threshold for formal CLAUDE.md promotion is min 3 vault-code data points (Phase 1 + Phase 2 + Phase 3 spike-related); Phase 1b counts toward the same set since it's vault-code.

### T0.1.9 Phase 3 Step 2a + 2b — closure record (preserved as historical anchor)

**Where you were when you woke up after 2a+2b:** working tree clean, `origin/main` at the Step 2a + 2b roll-forward commit. Step 2a + 2b shipped + sustained CI green verified.

**Step 2c scope (T0.1.9 final close gate):** Add `windows-latest` to the CI matrix on `clippy` + `build-and-test` jobs (`fmt` is OS-agnostic, stays single-runner). ORT setup step gated on `runner.os == 'Windows'` invoking `scripts/setup-dev-env.ps1`. ORT dylib + model + tokenizer cache via `actions/cache@v4` keyed on `runner.os` so Windows fixtures are isolated from Linux fixtures. All four DoD gates green on Windows runner.

**Step 2c tactical patch shape (proposed; confirm at plan time):**
```yaml
clippy:
  strategy:
    matrix:
      os: [ubuntu-latest, windows-latest]
  runs-on: ${{ matrix.os }}
  steps:
    - if: runner.os == 'Linux'
      uses: jlumbroso/free-disk-space@main
      with:
        large-packages: true
        docker-images: true
    # ... existing steps ...

build-and-test:
  strategy:
    matrix:
      os: [ubuntu-latest, windows-latest]
  runs-on: ${{ matrix.os }}
  steps:
    - if: runner.os == 'Linux'
      uses: jlumbroso/free-disk-space@main
      with:
        large-packages: true
        docker-images: true
    # ... checkout + protoc + toolchain + rust-cache (all OS-agnostic) ...
    - name: Cache vault-embedding test fixtures
      uses: actions/cache@v4
      id: vault-embedding-fixtures
      with:
        path: crates/vault-embedding/test-fixtures
        key: vault-embedding-fixtures-${{ runner.os }}-${{ hashFiles('scripts/setup-dev-env.sh', 'scripts/setup-dev-env.ps1', 'crates/vault-embedding/src/integrity.rs') }}
    - name: Provision vault-embedding test fixtures (Linux)
      if: steps.vault-embedding-fixtures.outputs.cache-hit != 'true' && runner.os == 'Linux'
      run: bash scripts/setup-dev-env.sh
    - name: Provision vault-embedding test fixtures (Windows)
      if: steps.vault-embedding-fixtures.outputs.cache-hit != 'true' && runner.os == 'Windows'
      run: pwsh scripts/setup-dev-env.ps1
      shell: pwsh
    - run: cargo build --workspace --all-targets
    - run: cargo test --workspace
```

**Notable Windows-specific concerns to validate at plan time:**
- **Strawberry Perl prerequisite** — `rusqlite` `bundled-sqlcipher-vendored-openssl` requires Perl at build time per ADR-006. CI on Windows needs `shogo82148/actions-setup-perl@v1` step or equivalent. Local Windows dev has Strawberry Perl via winget.
- **PROTOC path on Windows** — `arduino/setup-protoc@v3` is OS-agnostic per its README, should work; verify at first run.
- **Line-ending CRLF on golden files** — none in suite currently per `git grep` of test fixtures, but worth grepping again if Step 2c surfaces a Windows-only test failure.
- **`tokio::io::duplex` round-trip timing** — Step 9's `full_initialize_round_trip_lists_four_tools_with_expected_names` could behave differently on Windows; if it flakes, root-cause investigation per the standing rule, NOT `#[cfg(unix)]` skip.

**Step 2c verification protocol:**
1. Push the workflow patch to `main` as the Step 2c commit.
2. Watch CI: BOTH `ubuntu-latest` AND `windows-latest` matrix entries should land `success` within ~30-50 minutes (Windows is typically slower for first-time builds without a populated `Swatinem/rust-cache@v2`).
3. **Run a follow-up commit** (HANDOFF roll-forward marking T0.1.9 fully shipped) and verify CI passes on that. **Two consecutive green matrix runs** = Step 2c shipped + T0.1.9 fully closed.

**Step 2c escalation surfaces:**
- Any existing test failing Windows-only — root-cause, NOT `#[cfg(unix)]` skip. Standing rule live.
- Strawberry Perl install failing in CI — fall back to `shogo82148/actions-setup-perl` with explicit version pin.
- Windows runner disk-space pressure (less than Linux but possible with full toolchain + workspace) — `jlumbroso/free-disk-space` is Linux-only; Windows alternative is `microsoft/setup-msbuild@v2`'s implicit cleanup, OR explicit `Remove-Item -Recurse -Force <path>` for Android NDK / unused VS components.

**Floor forecast for Step 2c:** **0 new tests.** Workspace stays at **364 + 2 ignored** on each matrix entry. Success metric: TWO consecutive green CI matrix runs (the Step 2c commit + a follow-up).

**T0.1.9 close metric:** Step 2c ships + sustained CI green across `[ubuntu-latest, windows-latest]` matrix on at least 2 consecutive commits. **T0.1.9 fully shipped at that point.** Three remaining V0.1 tasks: T0.1.10 (vault-app wiring + adversarial integration forward-pointer + retrieval perf-gate investigation candidate + deferred Phase 4 integration smoke), T0.1.11 (vault-tauri minimal UI + ADR-010 compensating controls + April 15 RCE class threat-surface revisit per ADR-026), T0.1.12 (founder dogfood e2e).

**CLAUDE.md candidate #8 — promotion gate live throughout T0.1.10:** Step 2a + 2b landed the first two concrete data points; **promotion to documented default still requires T0.1.10 early-commit data points** to demonstrate the pattern holds across non-CI-infra work. Don't promote until the candidate has demonstrated it works for vault-code commits, not just CI workflow changes.

### T0.1.9 Phase 3 Step 2a — closure record (preserved as historical anchor)

**Step 2a was the load-bearing prerequisite to fix Linux CI disk-space exhaustion at the `libduckdb-sys` archive step.** CI had been silently red for 22 commits since 2026-04-30 13:40 UTC; see "## CI Discipline Recovery — 2026-05-03 finding" section above for the full timeline + discipline-gap acknowledgment. Step 2a was the load-bearing prerequisite: until CI build succeeded on Linux, Step 2b (verify vault-embedding tests) and Step 2c (Windows matrix) could not ship.

**Pre-confirmed state (no verify-before-write needed for this step):**
- Workflow file: `.github/workflows/ci.yml` (3 jobs: `fmt` / `clippy` / `build-and-test`).
- Failure mode: `cargo:warning=ar: ... libduckdb.a: ... No space left on device` followed by `error occurred in cc-rs: ... exit status: 1` and `##[error]Process completed with exit code 101.`
- Last green run: `T0.1.6b` at 2026-04-30 11:48 UTC (run `25163659770`).
- Failure occurs in both `clippy` (via `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets`) and `build-and-test` (via `cargo build --workspace --all-targets`) — same root cause; both compile `libduckdb-sys`.

**Step 2a tactical fix (recommended):** add `jlumbroso/free-disk-space@main` action at the top of the `clippy` + `build-and-test` jobs. This is the standard tactic for GitHub-hosted ubuntu runners: removes unused tooling (~15-20GB recovered) — `/usr/share/dotnet` (~1.6GB), `/usr/share/swift`, `/opt/ghc`, `/usr/local/lib/android` (~14GB), `/usr/local/share/boost`, etc. Should provide ample headroom for `libduckdb.a` archive plus the rest of the workspace.

**Step 2a workflow patch shape (proposed; confirm at plan time):**
```yaml
clippy:
  runs-on: ubuntu-latest
  steps:
    - uses: jlumbroso/free-disk-space@main         # <-- NEW
      with:
        # large-package removals, keep tool-cache for actions/cache
        large-packages: true
        docker-images: true
    - uses: actions/checkout@v6
    # ... existing steps ...

build-and-test:
  runs-on: ubuntu-latest
  steps:
    - uses: jlumbroso/free-disk-space@main         # <-- NEW (mirror of clippy)
      with:
        large-packages: true
        docker-images: true
    - uses: actions/checkout@v6
    # ... existing steps ...
```

The `fmt` job doesn't need it — it doesn't compile vault-storage / DuckDB.

**Step 2a fallback if disk-cleanup alone is insufficient:** add `CARGO_PROFILE_DEV_DEBUG=line-tables-only` to the workflow `env:` block. This shrinks debug-info artefact size dramatically (often 2-3× smaller `target/debug`), at the cost of slightly less verbose backtraces. Acceptable for CI; local dev keeps full debug info.

**Step 2a verification protocol:**
1. Push the workflow patch to `main` as the Step 2a commit.
2. Watch CI: `gh run list --workflow=ci.yml -L 1` should show `success` within ~25-30 minutes.
3. **Run a follow-up no-op commit** (e.g., a HANDOFF roll-forward marking 2a shipped) and verify CI also passes on that. **One green run is not sufficient** — disk-pressure regressions can oscillate; two consecutive greens indicate stable margin.
4. Only after both green runs is Step 2a considered shipped + verified.

**Anticipated Step 2a contract surfaces (pre-empting per the contract-surface-anticipation pattern):**
- **(a) `jlumbroso/free-disk-space` step ordering.** Recommendation: BEFORE `actions/checkout@v6` so the cleanup runs on the freshly-allocated runner before any repo content lands. Alternative is after-checkout if there's a dependency (none expected). Decide at plan time only if a step ordering issue surfaces.
- **(b) `CARGO_PROFILE_DEV_DEBUG` fallback gating.** Recommendation: don't include in initial patch; only add if 2a's first attempt fails. Reduces blast radius — if the disk-cleanup alone works, debug-info size stays full for CI parity with local dev.
- **(c) `large-packages: true` + `docker-images: true` flags.** Recommendation: enable both; they're the heaviest categories in the action's removal list. Other flags (`tool-cache`, `swap-storage`) carry small risk of breaking other CI infrastructure — keep defaults.

**Step 2a escalation surfaces (standing rule live):**
- Disk-cleanup runs but the build still fails on disk space — escalate to fallback strategy (`CARGO_PROFILE_DEV_DEBUG`, or `cargo build --tests` instead of `--all-targets`, or `Swatinem/rust-cache@v2` configuration changes).
- CI passes on the 2a commit but fails on the follow-up no-op commit — disk margin is borderline; escalate to fallback.
- `jlumbroso/free-disk-space` itself fails (action breaks, deprecated, etc.) — research alternatives (`AdityaGarg8/remove-unwanted-software`, manual `rm -rf /opt/ghc /usr/local/lib/android` etc.).
- ANY existing test fails on Linux CI now that build succeeds — that's a Step 2b finding (the original priority-zero question), but it surfacing during Step 2a means escalate immediately.

**Floor forecast for Step 2a:** **0 new tests.** Workspace stays at **364 + 2 ignored**. Success metric: TWO consecutive green CI runs (the Step 2a commit + a follow-up).

**Step 2a close → Step 2b begins:** Step 2b runs the original priority-zero investigation that started this whole thread — does vault-embedding's panic-loudly-on-missing-fixtures path actually fire on CI now that build succeeds? Three sub-outcomes from the original framing still apply at Step 2b time, but now answerable empirically because builds complete.

#### T0.1.9 Phase 3 Step 2b — outline (after 2a ships)

Verify vault-embedding actual test behavior on Linux now that build succeeds. Read the full CI test log post-Step-2a; search for `embedding_tests::*` names. Three sub-outcomes:
- **(i)** Tests run + pass somehow. Need to understand HOW fixtures land on the runner (`.gitignore` excludes `test-fixtures/`, so they're not checked in). Document the mechanism.
- **(ii)** Tests run + fail-loud on missing fixtures. Add a Linux ORT-setup step parallel to the Windows one (via `scripts/setup-dev-env.sh`).
- **(iii)** Tests don't run at all. Check Cargo.toml `[lib]` / `[[test]]` gating in vault-embedding, or `--exclude` flags in workflow YAML. If excluded, decide: keep exclusion + ADR documenting why, OR remove + add fixture setup.

#### Step 4 work breakdown (shipped at `6515f31` — preserved as canonical record)

To un-ignore Step 3's `(c)` test + close the audit/observability infrastructure, Step 4 shipped:

1. **Define `ToolInvokeDetails` struct** in vault-mcp (`crates/vault-mcp/src/audit.rs`). Schema per ADR-024 (HANDOFF.md lines 770–790, T0.1.9_PLAN.md §5 line 161 + §6.2 rule 2 line 189) — *quote the ADR, do not paraphrase*:
   - Common fields: `tool: &'static str`, `duration_ms: u64`, `result_count: u32`, `boundary_count: u32`, `error: Option<ToolInvokeError>`
   - Search-only `Option<T>` fields with `#[serde(skip_serializing_if = "Option::is_none")]` so they're ABSENT (not `null`) on write/update/delete per Q1: `max_results: Option<u32>`, `score_threshold: Option<f32>`, `include_archived: Option<bool>`, `query_length: Option<u32>`.
   - `ToolInvokeError` is `#[serde(tag = "type", content = "detail")]` enum with one variant per ADR-024's mapping table row (`AccessDenied` / `DimensionMismatch` / `ModelIntegrityFailed` / `Storage` / `Embedding` / `Retrieval` / `InvalidInput`). Variant idents PascalCase; serde uses them as-is for `"type"`. Per-variant detail shapes per ADR-024 lines 787–790. Plus an `Internal { category, message }` variant for ADR-024-silent VaultError variants (collapsing `Llm` / `Crypto` / `Io` / etc. — privacy-preserving default until ADR-024 is amended).
   - Canonical sorted-key JSON via `ToolInvokeDetails::to_canonical_json` — uses `BTreeMap` at every nesting level so audit-chain hashing is deterministic per BRD §11.9.2.
2. **Add `Adapter::append_tool_invoke_audit(details: ToolInvokeDetails) -> VaultResult<()>`** to the trait (`crates/vault-mcp/src/adapter.rs`).
3. **Update `StubAdapter` + `DimMismatchAdapter`** in `tests/common/mod.rs` — add `Mutex<Vec<ToolInvokeDetails>>` recording field; `append_tool_invoke_audit` pushes into it; expose `recorded_audits()` method for assertions.
4. **Wire `tool_search` body** with: snapshot typed-param fields BEFORE handler dispatch (the handler moves params into a `RetrievalQuery`) → `let start = Instant::now();` → handler dispatch → `let duration_ms = start.elapsed().as_millis() as u64;` → build `ToolInvokeDetails` (mapping `VaultError` to `error.type` + variant-specific `detail` fields per ADR-024 via `ToolInvokeError::from_vault_error`) → emit `tracing::info!(target: "vault_mcp::tool_invoke", ...)` FIRST per Q5/Q6 (operational log fires regardless of audit-store health) → `self.adapter.append_tool_invoke_audit(details).await?;` (authoritative audit chain) → return result. The tracing-before-audit ordering is a small (F1)-style refinement vs the original work-breakdown ordering (audit-then-tracing); preserves the contract while ensuring tracing fires on audit-store failure.
5. **Un-ignore `dimension_mismatch_audit_row_pins_full_detail`**, replace `todo!()` with assertions on `recorded_audits()` at BOTH the typed-Rust level (`ToolInvokeError::DimensionMismatch { expected: 384, actual: 256 }`) AND the canonical-JSON wire level (`error.type == "DimensionMismatch"`, `error.detail.expected == 384`, `error.detail.actual == 256`) per ADR-024 nested shape. Also pin the absent-vs-null invariant for `score_threshold` (search call passed `None` → must NOT serialise as `"score_threshold": null`).
6. **Convert `vault_error_to_mcp` to exhaustive match** per Step 3 sanity-check #4 carryover. Read every `VaultError` variant; map each deliberately per ADR-024 mapping table — `AccessDenied` and `ModelIntegrityFailed` advance from the prior `-32602`-via-catch-all to ADR-024 line 764/766's locked `-32001` access-denied code. ADR-024-silent variants (`NotFound` / `Llm` / `Crypto` / `Io` / etc.) preserve prior catch-all behaviour with explicit per-variant arms, so adding a new `VaultError` variant becomes a compile error here.

**Step 4 expected test delta**: +1 active (un-ignored from Step 3) + 6 new audit unit tests in `audit::tests` → workspace **339 passing + 2 ignored** (perf gates). The +6 audit unit tests pin the wire format at the type level (canonical key ordering, search-fields-absent on write, DimensionMismatch nested shape, from-VaultError mapping) so future changes to the typed struct can't silently break ADR-024 conformance.

**Reconciliation note (2026-05-02):** the prior text of this work breakdown described `ToolInvokeError` as a flat `{ kind, expected, actual }` shape — that paraphrase drifted from ADR-024's locked nested `{ type, detail }` shape (HANDOFF.md lines 786–790 + T0.1.9_PLAN.md §5 line 161 + §6.2 rule 2 line 189). ADR-024 stays unchanged; the work-breakdown text was reconciled to quote the ADR contract directly. New feedback memory: "Quote locked artefacts, don't paraphrase" — operational doc text saying "per ADR-X" must match the cited artefact verbatim or quote it, never paraphrase.

### Locked-into-code invariants any V0.2+ work must respect

These are the design decisions T0.1.6 ships that downstream tasks need to honour:

- `RetryQueue::poll_due` orders by `(sequence_id ASC, next_attempt_at ASC)` — FIFO per memory_id. Don't change without amending ADR-017.
- `is_permanent` covers `DimensionMismatch / AccessDenied / Storage(msg).contains("schema")`. The orchestrator validates dim + boundary at `write_memory` entry so these classes shouldn't reach the queue (load-bearing precondition for the lockstep contract).
- `MAX_RETRY_QUEUE_DEPTH = 10_000`. T0.2.x sweep impl MUST check `RetryQueue::len()` before each re-enqueue to avoid blowing past the cap.
- `MAX_ATTEMPTS = 8`, schedule `1/2/4/8/16/30/60/120` seconds, ±25% jitter band.
- `dead_letter.resolution` strings exactly: `'retried_succeeded' | 'retried_failed' | 'acknowledged' | 'auto_recovered'`.
- `LAST_ERROR_MAX_BYTES = FAILURE_REASON_MAX_BYTES = 4096`.
- `JitterSource: Send + Sync` so the worker future is spawnable.
- `VectorStore::validate_readable` + `GraphStore::validate_readable` MUST exercise data-decode, not metadata (ADR-018).
- `VectorStore::contains(id)` is the divergence-detector's existence check — implementations should make it O(1) per id.
- `StorageBackend::open` returns `Ok` with `DegradedMode` on validation failure, never `Err`. T0.1.10 / T0.1.11 surface the degraded flag to the user.
- The cascading retry worker is owned by T0.1.10 (`Application::start`): it constructs `tokio::sync::watch::channel(false)`, spawns `worker.run(rx)`, and signals cancel from `Application::shutdown`.

**Pace caution carried forward:** T0.1.6 is the highest-stakes integration in V0.1. C1b adversarial tests + standard CRUD all green; C2 integration-tests against the orchestrator + the planted-divergence scenarios from Phase A Q5. The hard-corruption case is already handled by C1b's eager `validate_readable`-on-open; C2 covers SOFT corruption (silent row drops, manifest drift) which the eager check can't see (LanceDB count is metadata-only).

**Tables still deferred to later tasks** (no scaffolding rule):
- `review_queue` — added at connector ingestion task (BRD §5.9)
- `sync_state` — added at T0.2.x (sync engine)
Each lands via a new numbered SQLite migration file. The migration runner already supports this and is regression-tested by `forward_migration_applies_next_version_only`.
